19:641:52950:18:18:64:547:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(Table 6). We also Önd that eliminating lagged house price growth as an additional predictor
19:642:53042:18:35:64:373:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:has little ináuence on the predictability results using beliefs.
19:643:53106:35:25:64:484:626:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:3.4  Do Credit Standards Cause Changes in House Prices?
19:644:53161:25:18:64:547:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In this section we consider a Önal hypothesis, namely that there was no genuine causality
19:645:53250:18:18:64:547:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:running from credit conditions to house price changes, despite the positive correlation between
19:646:53345:18:18:64:547:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the two. Instead, the causality ran entirely in the other direction, i.e., from rising home prices to
19:647:53446:18:18:64:546:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:greater credit extension in the boom, and conversely from falling house prices to a constriction of
19:648:53545:18:18:64:546:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:credit during the bust. This reverse causality story is often associated with models where beliefs
19:649:53643:18:18:64:546:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:play an important role. For example, exuberant expectations about future house prices might
19:650:53734:18:18:64:546:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:have been the singular driving force behind rising house prices and relaxed credit conditions. If
19:651:53831:18:18:64:547:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:so, shocks to credit conditions that are mutually uncorrelated with house price shocks should
19:652:53924:18:18:64:249:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:not have an impact on house prices.
19:653:53959:18:18:82:547:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To address this question we identify exogenous variation in our measure of credit conditions,
19:654:54052:18:18:64:547:421:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:-CSt, and relate it to home price growth-ptusing a structural VAR (SVAR). To identify
19:655:54137:18:18:64:547:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:exogenous variation, we employ theshock-restrictedSVAR approach of Ludvigson, Ma, and
19:656:54222:18:17:64:546:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Ng (2015) and Ludvigson, Ma, and Ng (2016) that permits set identiÖcation of the structural
19:657:54313:17:18:64:546:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shocks under assumptions that are typically weaker than those required for point identiÖcation.
19:658:54408:18:18:64:547:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Here we provide only a brief description of the identiÖcation strategy and refer the reader to
19:659:54502:18:18:64:186:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:those papers for details.
19:660:54527:18:18:82:547:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The structural shocks of interest are the mutually uncorrelated innovations in the SVAR
19:661:54614:18:18:64:547:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:variables-CStand-pt. In this paper we focus on identifying a shock to credit standards
19:662:54700:18:18:64:547:278:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:-CStand tracing out its a§ects on house price growth-pt.6The single identifying assump-
19:663:54787:18:18:64:547:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tion we make is that changes in the composition of mortgages, i.e., toward non-conforming
19:664:54876:18:18:64:546:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loans and away from conforming loans, should be informative about credit standard shocks.
19:665:54965:18:18:64:546:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This is implemented by requiring that a positive credit standard structural shock (i.e., an eas-
19:666:55061:18:18:64:547:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ing of standards) must exhibit a minimum (lower bound) correlation with the quarterly log
19:667:55150:18:18:64:546:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:di§erence in the ratioABS=GSE;a variable that is external to the SVAR. We refer to this as
19:668:55240:18:18:64:547:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ashock-based external variable constraint, where the parameter-sets the lower bound of the
19:669:55330:18:18:64:547:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:correlation. Although this approach has the áavor of an external instrumental variable (IV) or
19:670:55424:18:16:78:547:134:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:6We do not focus on identifying exogenous variation in house price growth to ask if a§ects-CSt. Most
19:671:55524:16:12:64:546:118:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:paradigms, even those for which belief shocks play no role but exogenous movements in credit conditions have
19:672:55632:12:12:64:546:106:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:quantitatively important causal consquences for house prices (e.g., Favilukis, Ludvigson, and Van Nieuwerburgh
19:673:55742:12:12:64:546:94:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:(2017)), would imply this reverse causality. This is because credit conditions themeselves also have an endoge-
19:674:55853:12:12:64:546:82:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:nous component that moves with the economic state and home values. These values in turn shift collateralized
19:675:55961:12:0:64:381:70:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:borrowing capacity and alter Önancing constraints and credit conditions.
20:676:56035:0:18:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:proxy SVAR identiÖcation strategy (e.g., Stock and Watson (2008); Mertens and Ravn (2014)),
20:677:56126:18:18:64:547:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:unlike the external IV approach, the external variable in this methodology isnotassumed to be
20:678:56219:18:18:64:546:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:exogenous (uncorrelated with house price shocks) as would be required of a valid IV. Instead,
20:679:56312:18:18:64:546:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:we only require the weaker assumption that the composition of mortgages is relevant for credit
20:680:56406:18:18:64:546:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:standards. It is because these restrictions are weaker that we do not achieve point identiÖca-
20:681:56500:18:18:64:547:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tion. The bounds of the identiÖed set may still be informative, however, a possibility we now
20:682:56593:18:18:64:122:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:investigate.
20:683:56605:18:18:82:547:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We use impulse response functions to understand the dynamic causal e§ects and propagating
20:684:56694:18:18:64:546:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:mechanisms of a credit standards shock. Figure 7 shows, in shaded areas, the identiÖed set of
20:685:56787:18:18:64:547:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:dynamic responses of quarterly real house price growth (in percent) to a one standard deviation
20:686:56882:18:18:64:547:535:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:increasein the credit standards shock, which constitutes an easing of lending standards. The
20:687:56974:18:17:64:547:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Figure shows the results for two values of the lower bound on the correlation constraint between
20:688:57070:17:18:64:547:500:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:-CSshocks an-ln(ABSt=GSEt):-= 0:07and-= 0:05. That is, in the top panel the credit
20:689:57152:18:18:64:547:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:standards shocks are required to have a correlation with-ln(ABSt=GSEt)of at least 7%, while
20:690:57243:18:18:64:355:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in the bottom panel this requirement is slackened to 5%.
20:691:57299:18:18:82:547:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Given that we have a set of solutions, the impulse responses present a range of estimated
20:692:57388:18:18:64:546:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:magnitudes of the e§ect of credit standard shocks on house price growth. But the bounds of
20:693:57478:18:18:64:546:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the set are su¢ ciently tight that they are still informative about the dynamic relationship of
20:694:57573:18:18:64:547:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:interest. At the highest end of the range, the results for-= 0:07indicate that a one-standard
20:695:57666:18:18:64:547:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:deviation shock to-CSincreases real quarterly house price growth by 1.4% on impact, or
20:696:57752:18:18:64:547:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:roughly 5.7% at an annual rate. At the lowest end of the range, a one-standard deviation shock
20:697:57846:18:18:64:547:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to-CSincreases real quarterly house price growth by roughly 0.8% on impact, or roughly
20:698:57932:18:18:64:547:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2% at an annual rate. These results are not highly sensitive to the value of-, though the sets
20:699:58028:18:18:64:547:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are invariably wider when the identifying restriction is slackened. In the bottom panel, which
20:700:58122:18:18:64:547:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:shows the results for-=  0:05, the high end of the range is roughly the same as in the top
20:701:58212:18:18:64:547:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:panel, but the low end is lower than in the top panel. In this case, the low end shows that a
20:702:58305:18:17:64:546:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:one-standard deviation shock to-CSincreases real quarterly house price growth by roughly
20:703:58393:17:18:64:546:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:0.6% on impact, or roughly 2.4% at an annual rate. Though these magnitudes are substantial
20:704:58483:18:18:64:546:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and well determined, the estimated persistence of the e§ects is less well determined. At least
20:705:58577:18:18:64:547:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:some solutions in the identiÖed set imply that the e§ects die out after 3 quarters, while others
20:706:58673:18:36:64:254:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:suggest much more persistent e§ects.
20:707:58709:36:30:64:166:141:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:4  Conclusion
20:708:58722:30:18:64:547:111:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We consider two potential driving forces of house price áuctuations, credit conditions and
20:709:58812:18:18:64:547:93:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:beliefs, using direct measures of these variables.  To measure credit conditions, we use the
20:710:58904:18:0:64:547:75:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Senior Loan O¢ cer Opinion Survey conducted by the Federal Reserve, which asks senior loan
21:711:58996:0:18:64:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:o¢ cers at banks to state whether their lending standards for purchase mortgages have eased
21:712:59087:18:18:64:547:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:or tightened relative to the previous quarter.  To measure beliefs, we study three separate
21:713:59178:18:18:64:546:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:household-level survey measures from the University of Michiganís Survey of Consumers that
21:714:59268:18:18:64:547:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ask speciÖcally about the respondentís view on home prices and a fourth measure based on
21:715:59356:18:18:64:546:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the index constructed by Soo (2018) that measures sentiment about housing using a textual
21:716:59445:18:18:64:546:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:analysis of major news publications. We combine these data with data on national house prices
21:717:59538:18:18:64:547:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:in order to compile a set of statistical facts on the empirical relationships among these variables
21:718:59637:18:18:64:177:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:at the aggregate level.
21:719:59660:18:18:82:547:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:We Önd that a relaxation of credit standards is positively related to the fraction of riskier
21:720:59753:18:18:64:547:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:non-conforming debt in total mortgage lending, while beliefs bear little empirical relation to
21:721:59847:18:18:64:546:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:this fraction. Credit conditions have statistically signiÖcant and economically important ex-
21:722:59940:18:17:64:547:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:planatory power for contemporaneous house price changes as well as predictive power for future
21:723:60034:17:18:64:547:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:house price changes, even after lagged house price changes and economic fundamentals such
21:724:60123:18:18:64:547:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:as interest rates and expected economic growth are controlled for. Two measures of beliefs
21:725:60213:18:18:64:547:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:have statistically signiÖcant explanatory power for contemporaneous house price changes once
21:726:60305:18:18:64:546:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:fundamentals are controlled for, though these measures explain substantially smaller fractions
21:727:60399:18:18:64:546:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the variation in house price growth than do credit standards. These are the Soo national
21:728:60490:18:18:64:547:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:housing media sentiment index, and the growth in the share of households in the SOC who
21:729:60577:18:18:64:546:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reported being optimistic about the housing market because they said house prices would fur-
21:730:60669:18:18:64:547:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:ther appreciate. We Önd little evidence that beliefs have importantpredictivepower for future
21:731:60762:18:18:64:547:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:house price changes, once credit conditions, fundamentals and lagged house price growth are
21:732:60853:18:18:64:546:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:controlled for. A structural VAR analysis implies that shocks to credit conditions have quan-
21:733:60946:18:18:64:547:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:titatively large dynamic causal e§ects on house price changes, especially in the short-run, with
21:734:61042:18:18:64:547:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:positive shocks (an easing of credit) driving up home values and negative shocks driving them
21:735:61135:18:0:64:94:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:down.

38:1258:83087:0:30:64:185:715:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:Online Appendix
38:1259:83102:30:26:64:173:685:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:Data Appendix
38:1260:83115:26:31:64:237:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This appendix discusses the data.
38:1261:83148:31:25:64:165:628:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:Credit Standards
38:1262:83164:25:18:64:546:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The Senior Loan O¢ cer Opinion Survey on Bank Lending Practices (SLOOS) provides qual-
38:1263:83250:18:18:64:547:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:itative and limited quantitative information on bank credit availability and loan demand, as
38:1264:83342:18:18:64:547:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:well as on evolving developments and lending practices in the U.S. loan markets. The FED
38:1265:83430:18:18:64:547:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:requires one or more senior loan o¢ cers at each respondent bank to complete the survey, up to
38:1266:83524:18:18:64:547:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:six times a year; however, the survey has typically been conducted only four times a year since
38:1267:83619:18:18:64:546:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1992. The current reporting panel consists of up to 80 large domestically chartered commercial
38:1268:83713:18:18:64:547:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks and up to 24 large U.S. branches and agencies of foreign banks. The minimum asset size
38:1269:83805:18:18:64:546:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:for panel institutions is $2 billions (this amount was reduced in 2012 from $3 billion). As of
38:1270:83899:18:18:64:546:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:March 31, 2017, the panel of domestic respondents contained 80 banks, 47 of which had assets
38:1271:83991:18:18:64:547:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of $20 billion or more. The assets of the panel banks totaled $11.8 trillion and accounted for
38:1272:84085:18:18:64:542:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:about 69 percent of the $17.0 trillion in total assets of all domestically chartered institutions.
38:1273:84183:18:18:82:547:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The FED seeks to limit the di¢ culty and quantitative content of survey questions. When
38:1274:84270:18:18:64:547:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:quantitative information is requested, respondents generally are asked to provide approximate
38:1275:84363:18:18:64:546:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:or rough estimates, usually in terms of percentages rather than dollar amounts. A respondent
38:1276:84455:18:17:64:547:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:may decline to answer a particular question when answering would entail excessive burden. The
38:1277:84548:17:18:64:547:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:FED distributes two versions of the survey, one to domestically chartered institutions and one
38:1278:84642:18:18:64:306:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:to U.S. branches and agencies of foreign banks.
38:1279:84689:18:18:82:547:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Since 2012, the FED maintains a panel of 80 banks (from 1981 to 2012, the FED maintained
38:1280:84777:18:18:64:546:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:a panel of 60 insured, domestically chartered commercial banks, before 1981 they were 120).
38:1281:84868:18:18:64:546:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:To ensure adequate geographic coverage, the survey panel of domestic banks spans all Federal
38:1282:84960:18:18:64:546:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Reserve Districts, while balancing the need to keep it heavily weighted toward the largest banks.
38:1283:85057:18:18:64:547:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:However, the panel also includes a fair number of large and medium-size regional banks, which
38:1284:85150:18:18:64:544:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:allows for a greater diversity of responses and provides a broader view of the banking system.
38:1285:85244:18:18:82:547:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In selecting the panel, the Fed generally imposes three constraints: (i)size: banks that
38:1286:85332:18:18:64:547:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:have less than $2 billion of total assets or for which commercial and industrial (C&I) loans
38:1287:85424:18:18:64:546:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are less than 5 % of total assets are eliminated from consideration, with a few exceptions,
38:1288:85515:18:18:64:546:136:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:(ii)geographic diversity: between two and ten banks are included from each district, (iii)
38:1289:85605:18:18:64:547:118:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:mutual independence: with some exceptions, a bank is eliminated from consideration if it
38:1290:85693:18:18:64:547:100:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is a subsidiary of a bank holding company that is already represented in the panel, because
38:1291:85784:18:17:64:547:82:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:its responses would likely not be independent of those of the related bank already providing
38:1292:85876:17:0:64:115:65:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:responses.
39:1293:85887:0:18:82:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The Fed tries to maintain a panel of U.S. branches and agencies of foreign banks. As of
39:1294:85974:18:18:64:546:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:March 2017, the panel included 23 institutions, 21 of which are located in the New York District.
39:1295:86071:18:18:64:547:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:In March 2017, the share of C&I loans held by respondent U.S. branches and agencies of foreign
39:1296:86165:18:18:64:546:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:banks ($187.7 billion) relative to that held by the universe of such institutions ($274.8 billion)

41:1384:91788:26:18:64:547:268:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:University of Michiganís Survey of Consumers - Price Expectations.The survey is
41:1385:91867:18:18:64:547:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:conducted each month to a minimum of 500 households. It contains approximately 50 core
41:1386:91953:18:18:64:547:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:questions, each of which tracks a di§erent aspect of consumer attitudes and expectations. The
41:1387:92046:18:18:64:546:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:samples for the Surveys of Consumers are statistically designed to be representative of all
41:1388:92137:18:18:64:546:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:American households. We are interested in the Index of Consumer Expectations which focuses
41:1389:92227:18:18:64:547:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:on: consumersíview of their own Önancial situation and their view of the general economy in
41:1390:92318:18:18:64:207:160:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the short and the long term
41:1391:92345:18:18:82:547:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The method used to select monthly nationally representative samples of persons is generally
41:1392:92436:18:17:64:547:124:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:referred to as random digit dialing (RDD) of cellular telephone numbers. However, any single
41:1393:92528:17:18:64:547:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:monthly sample consists of two parts, an RDD sample of cell telephone subscribers selected in
41:1394:92621:18:18:64:546:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that month and a sample of RDD sample cell telephone subscribers who completed interviews
41:1395:92710:18:0:64:547:71:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:six months previously. The latter is referred to as the re-contact sample, and the former the
42:1396:92804:0:30:64:371:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:RDD sample7. The questions we focus on are the following:
42:1397:92861:30:18:82:547:685:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f3:Question A24a:What do you think will happen to the prices of homes like yours in your

42:1399:92990:31:28:79:219:636:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1. increase at a rapid rate?
42:1400:93018:28:28:79:240:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2. increase at a moderate rate?

42:1404:93136:45:18:82:547:479:12:g_d0_f33:12:g_d0_f3:Question A24b:By about what percent do you expect prices of homes like yours in your
42:1405:93220:18:17:64:408:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:community to go (up/down), on average, over the next 12 months?
42:1406:93283:17:30:182:221:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Percent
42:1407:93290:30:18:82:547:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:All responses are coded in an open-ended format, with any answers outside of the range
42:1408:93376:18:18:64:244:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:-95% to +95% truncated to-95%.
42:1409:93406:18:31:82:424:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Some types of adjustments are made to the response distributions:
42:1410:93471:31:18:79:547:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1.Imputations for missing information:There are three missing data codes that are
42:1411:93552:18:18:94:547:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:used to document the type and extent of the missing information to the questions on
42:1412:93635:18:18:94:547:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:price expectations. First,NAindicates that no information is available. In most cases,
42:1413:93721:18:18:94:547:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:it reáects a respondentís refusal to answer the question. This type of missing data is
42:1414:93807:18:18:94:547:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:relatively uncommon. Second,DK IFsigniÖes that in response to the Örst question on
42:1415:93889:18:18:94:547:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the expected direction of change in prices, the respondent replied that they did not know
42:1416:93978:18:18:94:547:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:whether prices would increase or decrease. This response reáects the respondentís lack
42:1417:94064:18:18:94:547:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of knowledge or understanding, and hence lacks any information content. This type of
42:1418:94148:18:17:94:546:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:missing data has also been relatively uncommon. Third,DK UP - DK DWsignify
42:1419:94222:17:18:94:547:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:that only partial information was obtained. The respondents indicated the direction they
42:1420:94310:18:18:94:547:168:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:expected prices to change but replied that they didnít know how much prices would
42:1421:94391:18:23:94:179:150:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:increase/decline.
42:1422:94408:23:18:94:547:127:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Respondents coded asNAorDK IFwere eliminated from the calculated estimates. By
42:1423:94486:18:18:94:547:109:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:excluding these cases, the implicit assumption is that the overall sample mean or median
42:1424:94574:18:18:94:336:91:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is the best estimate of the missing information.
42:1425:94622:18:0:78:391:73:7:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:7Seehttps://data.sca.isr.umich.edu/fetchdoc.php?docid=57449.
43:1426:94683:0:18:94:547:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The partial information codesDK UPandDK DWprovide important information
43:1427:94754:18:18:94:547:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:about the direction of expected change in prices (but not the extent of expected change).
43:1428:94843:18:18:94:547:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:The usual procedure is to impute the mean/median increase or decrease calculated among
43:1429:94929:18:18:94:547:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the complete data cases. Rather than imputing apoint estimateof the mean or median, a
43:1430:95014:18:18:94:547:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:distribution of responses is imputed whose mean/median is identical to the point estimate.
43:1431:95104:18:18:94:547:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This is done by distributing the DK UP and DK DW cases across all response codes in
43:1432:95187:18:27:94:389:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the same proportions as cases with complete information.
43:1433:95243:27:18:79:546:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.Truncation of outliers:At each step in the data collection process, all extreme values
43:1434:95331:18:18:94:547:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:are veriÖed: interviewers are instructed to probe all unusually large responses, asking
43:1435:95418:18:18:94:547:544:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:respondents to conÖrm their answers; at each subsequent step in data processing all large
43:1436:95507:18:18:94:547:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:values are subjected to special checking and editing procedures to verify that all responses
43:1437:95599:18:18:94:547:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:were accurately transcribed. The remaining extreme values are assumed to accurately
43:1438:95682:18:18:94:547:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:reáect the respondentíanswers. The methodology favors the truncation rather than the
43:1439:95766:18:35:94:247:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:elimination of extreme values.
43:1440:95796:35:17:64:547:437:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:University of Michiganís Survey of Consumers - Buying Condition Index.Because
43:1441:95873:17:18:64:547:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of the availability problem with the price expectations data, we use another measure provided

47:1592:104985:0:18:64:546:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:loans, balloon mortgage loans, interest-only mortgage loans, mortgage loans with prepayment

47:1599:105615:18:18:64:547:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:sold with lender recourse or subject to other third-party risk-sharing arrangements, or were
47:1600:105707:18:18:64:547:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:acquired by Fannie Mae on a negotiated bulk basis. For manually underwritten loans, Fannie
47:1601:105797:18:18:64:547:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Maeís maximum total PTI ratio is 36% of the borrowerís stable monthly income. The maximum
47:1602:105886:18:18:64:546:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:can be exceeded up to 45% if the borrower meets the credit score and reserve requirements re-

47:1605:106158:18:18:64:547:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the loan caseÖle will receive an ineligible recommendation. We get these PTI ratios from the
47:1606:106250:18:0:64:244:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:Fannie Mae Single Family Dataset.
48:1607:106285:0:26:64:212:715:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:Bootstrap Procedure
48:1608:106304:26:18:64:547:689:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This appendix describes our bootstrap procedure. We employ two approaches that we refer to as
48:1609:106397:18:18:64:547:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the parametric and non-parametric bootstrap. The distinction refers to how serial dependence
48:1610:106489:18:18:64:547:653:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:is modeled. In the Örst approach, serial dependence is speciÖed using a parametric model. In
48:1611:106581:18:18:64:546:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the second approach, it is speciÖed using a block bootstrap procedure. For both approaches,
48:1612:106672:18:30:64:335:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:the general linear model we consider is the following:
48:1613:106726:30:29:256:547:587:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:yt=\f0+\f\f\f0xxxt+-yt(A1)
48:1614:106752:29:18:64:547:558:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:wherexxxtis a vector of regressors. In some speciÖcationsxxxtwill be a scalar; in other cases, it will
48:1615:106854:18:18:64:547:540:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:be multidimensional. We are interested in the distribution of thet-statistic for each element
48:1616:106947:18:18:64:547:522:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:of\f\f\f, under the null that\f\f\f= 0. We use ì*îto denote statistics and data generated from the
48:1617:107045:18:35:64:487:504:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:bootstrap procedure, while ìhatsîdenote statistics estimated from historical data.
48:1618:107127:35:26:64:316:469:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:Algorithm 1: Parametric Bootstrap
48:1619:107160:26:30:64:299:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This algorithm consists of the following steps:
48:1620:107207:30:18:79:547:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1. Generate data under the null that\f\f\f= 0. Estimate the time series regression in (A2) and

51:1835:109687:26:18:64:547:689:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:This procedure uses block bootstrap sampling to capture serial dependence in the data. We
51:1836:109776:18:18:64:547:671:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:choose the block length following the recommendation of Hall, Horowitz, and Jing (1995) who

51:1838:109962:18:18:64:546:635:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tion isl_T1=4; also see Horowitz (2003). For the results reported in the text, we use a block
51:1839:110055:18:18:64:547:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:length exactly equal toT1=4= 3, but we check the robustness of our results to lengths of 2 and
51:1840:110149:18:18:64:547:599:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:5 and Önd little di§erence in the resulting distributions and conÖdence sets. This algorithm
